  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c3a895da-fa17-412a-ae5c-9b41b1fe1568'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer3672706360201537023">Sixteen-year-old Clariel is not adjusting well to her new life in the city of Belisaere, the capital of the Old Kingdom. She misses roaming freely within the forests of Estwael, and she feels trapped within the stone city walls. And in Belisaere she is forced to follow the plans, plots and demands of everyone, from her parents to her maid, to the sinister Guildmaster Kilp.</span>
  <span id="freeText3672706360201537023" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Clariel is not adjusting well to her new life in the city of Belisaere, the capital of the Old Kingdom. She misses roaming freely within the forests of Estwael, and she feels trapped within the stone city walls. And in Belisaere she is forced to follow the plans, plots and demands of everyone, from her parents to her maid, to the sinister Guildmaster Kilp. Clariel can see her freedom slipping away. It seems too that the city itself is descending into chaos, as the ancient rules binding Abhorsen, King and Clayr appear to be disintegrating.<br /><br />With the discovery of a dangerous Free Magic creature loose in the city, Clariel is given the chance both to prove her worth and make her escape. But events spin rapidly out of control. Clariel finds herself more trapped than ever, until help comes from an unlikely source. But the help comes at a terrible cost. Clariel must question the motivations and secret hearts of everyone around her - and it is herself she must question most of all.<br /><br />[This is an alternative edition of ASIN B00KK6FK40]</span>

    <a title="Kcatty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/693251-kcatty"><img alt="Kcatty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294097224p2/693251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102813095?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kcatty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kcatty" href="/user/show/693251-kcatty">Kcatty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/693251-kcatty?shelf=nix">nix</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/693251-kcatty?shelf=r-done">r-done</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102813095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16364926360327670058">This book was hard to read, but not for the reasons you’re probably thinking of.<br/><br/>Garth Nix’s writing was the best it’s ever been. It’s not my favorite style, but I like it nonetheless. The plot was engaging, the pacing was good – not fantastic, but not widely variable or unbearably slow – and the worldbuilding was, as usual, wonderful.<br/><br/>This was hard for me to read because Clariel reminded me a lot of myself when I was younger.<br/><br/>My parents took me out of the public school system after 8th grade and e</span>
  <span id="freeText16364926360327670058" style="display:none">This book was hard to read, but not for the reasons you’re probably thinking of.<br /><br />Garth Nix’s writing was the best it’s ever been. It’s not my favorite style, but I like it nonetheless. The plot was engaging, the pacing was good – not fantastic, but not widely variable or unbearably slow – and the worldbuilding was, as usual, wonderful.<br /><br />This was hard for me to read because Clariel reminded me a lot of myself when I was younger.<br /><br />My parents took me out of the public school system after 8th grade and enrolled me in a private school for 9th grade. They destroyed my social support and threw my academics off-track, and I’ve never let them forget that they deliberately ignored me and my protests through the whole process.<br /><br />The whole time I was reading this book, every time Clariel expressed her single-minded desire to go back home, it was very hard to not throw all my support behind her. I was never quiet about the fact that I didn’t want to be in private school; it was obnoxious and unkind to the friends I made that year, but for me leaving was the most important thing in the world, and I was never going to let anyone forget that.<br /><br />But what I learned at that school was that I didn’t know myself as well as I thought I did. When you spend your whole life in one environment, it’s very hard to separate yourself from your surroundings. And for all that we strive to make our environments suit us, we often grow more, and learn more about ourselves, in unfamiliar settings.<br /><br />Many of the assumptions I’d made about myself through life were proven wrong in 9th grade – that I couldn’t make friends, that I could be a one-woman island against the world, but also the idea that I should force myself to talk to people even when I wasn’t comfortable. Hell, I developed most of my social skills that year.<br /><br />So it was very, very hard for me to not root for Clariel in her quest to get back to the forests; it was equally hard for me to disapprove of her parents’ arguments that she would grow to like Belisaere, make friends and adapt to the new environment.<br /><br />I don’t agree with the people whose reactions to the book were negative because Clariel’s character was selfish, impulsive and unwise for the decisions she made and the beings she trusted. Not because it’s untrue (it is very true, in fact), but because I myself contemplated doing things relatively as drastic as what she did, and if I’d had more backbone and been less indecisive, I would have gone through with them – and they would had backfired as dramatically as Clariel’s actions did.<br /><br />And that’s what I think Garth Nix was trying to portray with this book: that period in every person’s life when they’re forced out of their comfort zone and into alien environments, forced to interact with new people; and how their reactions and ultimate success or failure with the change is influenced so much by who they are and who surrounds them and does, or doesn’t, support them.<br /><br />And part of the reason I think this worked so well was that this book is the other side of the Old Kingdom Universe coin, a foil to the first three books. <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/518848.Sabriel__Abhorsen___1_" title="Sabriel (Abhorsen, #1) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabriel</a>
</i>, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47624.Lirael__Abhorsen___2_" title="Lirael (Abhorsen, #2) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Lirael</a>
</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/334643.Abhorsen__Abhorsen___3_" title="Abhorsen (Abhorsen, #3) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Abhorsen</a>
</i> tell the stories of young women who haven’t found their places yet, who are thrown out of their comfort zones into truly brutal environments and forced with very little support to discover their destinies and save the world – and they succeed spectacularly.<br /><br />But the exact opposite happens to Clariel – the environment she’s forced into isn’t hostile; she has a multitude of possible friends and mentors, numerous new skills she could learn and become competent at. The possibilities are endless, her future completely in her hands.<br /><br />And the tragedy of it all is that, even with all this potential, Clariel is still completely isolated and fails miserably at anything she attempts. Her friends and mentors have their own agendas; she is given no time to adjust to Belisaere before being given responsibility far beyond her capabilities; and her own stubborn loner personality prevents her from reaching out to the right people, asking for help at the right times – even recognizing possible dangers until it’s too late. Out of the perfect situation is created the perfect storm.<br /><br />So of <i>course</i> the pacing of the story is going to be rough, of <i>course</i> the best characters are going to be underutilized – if the story had been steadier, if the right characters had been present, then Clariel wouldn’t have turned out the way she did.<br /><br />The people who are supposed to be role models, whose jobs it is to take care of the Kingdom and its people, are so wrapped up in their own wants, their own personal grudges, that a very stable situation turns to shit in a matter of weeks. They have all the resources, all the energy and all the time in the world to do their jobs, and they waste all of it completely. And Clariel is caught in the middle of this whole mess, disoriented and alone, <i>and the story shows that</i>.<br /><br />Another complaint I saw was that this wasn’t a whole story, that it felt like a rough draft that was missing a good conclusion and a good protagonist. And they’re right, this wasn’t a complete story and it did lack a sympathetic protagonist.<br /><br /><i>Clariel</i> isn’t a full story: it’s a snippet, a couple weeks pulled from history to help us understand how things were and how they came to be what they are now. No, the story didn’t finished: we didn’t get to see all of Clariel’s history, only the beginning of her descent into the horrifying Greater Dead creature we saw in <i>Lirael</i> and <i>Abhorsen</i>.<br /><br /><i>But that’s the point</i>. Nix purposefully leaves the rest of the story untold, forcing us to imagine how far both Clariel/Chlorr and the Old Kingdom have come in the intervening 600 years. One of my complaints about <i>Sabriel</i> is that we were told very little about how the Old Kingdom was in Touchstone’s time, forced (again) to imagine how it was and how it came to be what it was in Sabriel’s time. I think <i>Clariel</i> fulfills that role – it creates a third point of reference so that we can better track the changes to the Old Kingdom over time.<br /><br />That’s why the book was so worldbuilding-heavy, and why Clariel’s story took a backseat at times to the machinations and worries of other characters. This book was the tale of a participant in a larger story, a few weeks during a minor crisis – in a history of the Old Kingdom, Clariel, daughter of Jaciel and Harven, would be a footnote, perhaps not even given a paragraph in the chapter of the 1300s AW.<br /><br />This story is completely Clariel’s, her point-of-view on full display and her experiences in detail. But it’s also not hers at all, because she’s only one cog in the greater political and magical machines of the Old Kingdom.<br /><br />So don’t be so hard on the book – it wasn’t supposed to be a regular book, and I don’t think it would’ve been any good if Nix had written it as such.<br /><br />*<br /><br />Pre-read obsessive updating has been deleted to save characters, but I've kept the art links.<br /><br /><a href="http://rengintumer.tumblr.com/post/24832336355/a-backlog-of-work-i-still-needed-to-post-i-kept" rel="nofollow noopener">Tons</a> <a href="http://sketchylizstifel.tumblr.com/post/93245667920/lirael-in-death-facing-the-ninth-gate" rel="nofollow noopener">of</a> <a href="http://chartermagic.tumblr.com/post/93152281560/hmm-i-did-do-a-red-orange-version-of-this-only-i" rel="nofollow noopener">art</a>! Also, the new cover artist, Sebastian Ciaffaglione, is <a href="http://sebastianciaffaglione.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">on tumblr</a>! He's been posting some <a href="http://sebastianciaffaglione.tumblr.com/tagged/garth-nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Old Kingdom art</a> along with original and other series' art. A <a href="https://twitter.com/S_Ciaffaglione/status/481651580488265729" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabriel sketch</a> and some <a href="https://twitter.com/S_Ciaffaglione/status/482062745341157376" rel="nofollow noopener">back cover monsters</a>. <a href="http://dreamingbeagle.tumblr.com/post/86571987228/some-linework-i-started-of-lirael-a-character" rel="nofollow noopener">Lirael</a> and <a href="http://ceruly.tumblr.com/post/86479688512" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabriel</a>. The <a href="https://twitter.com/Enchantedbooks/status/446274377521577984" rel="nofollow noopener">British hardcover art</a> for <i>Across The Wall</i>, <a href="http://catandcrown.tumblr.com/post/79913211410/the-clayr-saw-me-the-wallmaker-made-me-the-king" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabriel</a>, <a href="http://jennathings.tumblr.com/post/20038941026/hey-everyone-i-drew-sabriel-this-is-the-first" rel="nofollow noopener">more Sabriel</a>, and <a href="http://chartermagic.tumblr.com/post/80603202713/the-nine-gates-of-death-from-sabriel-by-garth" rel="nofollow noopener">all nine gates of Death</a>, traveled by Lirael and illustrated by Laura Tolton the Great. <a href="http://chartermagic.tumblr.com/tagged/garth-nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Art on Laura Tolton the Great</a>'s tumblr and <a href="http://whenthedeaddowalk.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">a whole blog of art</a>. And to the user named Astarael: I <a href="http://kasutera.tumblr.com/post/74285658181/the-weeper" rel="nofollow noopener">shall share</a> <a href="http://fragmentedvisions.tumblr.com/post/63359026409/prettywords-lirael-garthnix-abhorsentrilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">with you</a> <a href="http://whenthedeaddowalk.tumblr.com/post/72606772815/maudthefish-working-on-designs-for-all-7" rel="nofollow noopener">creations regarding</a> <a href="http://whenthedeaddowalk.tumblr.com/post/62533170710/nauticalavenger-phew-okay-im-gonna-sleep-now" rel="nofollow noopener">our shared bell</a> (and my tumblr url). Will I do this for anybody else with a bell-themed goodreads name? No. Nobody talks about the bells at all, it's annoying. And lastly, <a href="https://twitter.com/kevinjaystanton/status/412695510252650496" rel="nofollow noopener">art</a>!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338978000?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471403866" href="/book/show/25418859-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338978000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2577172520462240249"><i> “Anyone can go into death” said Mogget, with a smirk. “Coming back again is the difficult part.” </i><br/><br/>I am loving this series so much! <br/>Clariel is a prequel to The Old Kingdom series, about 600 years earlier. <br/><br/>Clariel likes her life, sure her parents could be a bit more caring and pay a bit more attention, but she’s got her Aunt Lemmin and the wonderful forest she loves to explore. <br/>So when her parents decide the family is going to up and move to Belisare, and send her to a ‘finishing school’ Clariel i</span>
  <span id="freeText2577172520462240249" style="display:none"><i> “Anyone can go into death” said Mogget, with a smirk. “Coming back again is the difficult part.” </i><br /><br />I am loving this series so much! <br />Clariel is a prequel to The Old Kingdom series, about 600 years earlier. <br /><br />Clariel likes her life, sure her parents could be a bit more caring and pay a bit more attention, but she’s got her Aunt Lemmin and the wonderful forest she loves to explore. <br />So when her parents decide the family is going to up and move to Belisare, and send her to a ‘finishing school’ Clariel is heartbroken. She cannot bear to be torn away from her beloved forest. <br /><br /><i> “Does the Walker choose the path, or the path the Walker?” </i><br /><br />School is no better. She is taught how to pour tea, and the correct way to introduce herself to other noble men and women, as well as the art of charter magic, something she has never thought much of before. <br /><br />Belisare is full of tension and political intrigue. The King has withdrawn from all duties, and the Governor has taken over without anyone really noticing or calling him out on it. <br />When everything blows up and things get cray, Clariel is moved to her grandfathers house - the current Abhorsen. But she knows it’s just another prison, another blockade keeping her from the forest she desires so badly, so Clariel plans to escape, by any means necessary. <br />Clariel is different to the previous books I’ve read in this series. There is less of the ‘death’ parts and less Charter magic. But there is more focus on free magic and the other side of things. <br />Overall I thoroughly enjoyed this one and I’m excited to jump into the final book! <br /><br /><i> “The most important thing is to be true to yourself, however you feel, and not try to feel or behave differently because you think you should, or someone has told you how you must feel.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2577172520462240249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_53605471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53605471" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53605471?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758627" href="/book/show/7489530-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=pacing-pacing-pacing">pacing-pacing-pacing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=needed-more-editor">needed-more-editor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=queer-stuff">queer-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53605471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17011492840897507806">First of all, let me get this out of the way: everyone calling Clariel - the character - names can shut the hell up. I'm pissed as hell at the number of people writing her off as a bitch, whiny, self-centered, etc., especially when that's the extent of their critique of the book. It smells of misogyny and it needs to stop.<br/><br/>Now, as for the book...<br/><br/>I've been waiting for this book for a long time - pretty much since I read the original trilogy and first came across rumors that this was in the works. </span>
  <span id="freeText17011492840897507806" style="display:none">First of all, let me get this out of the way: everyone calling Clariel - the character - names can shut the hell up. I'm pissed as hell at the number of people writing her off as a bitch, whiny, self-centered, etc., especially when that's the extent of their critique of the book. It smells of misogyny and it needs to stop.<br /><br />Now, as for the book...<br /><br />I've been waiting for this book for a long time - pretty much since I read the original trilogy and first came across rumors that this was in the works. It had a high standard to meet, as the Abhorsen books are some of the best YA I've ever read. The thing is, from the time the first few chapters came out as a sampler, I've had an inkling that this wasn't going to match its predecessors. And, sadly, I was right.<br /><br />I came out of this book with the strong impression that I'd read an early draft, not a finished product. It has a lot of the hallmarks of an under-revised work: too many characters who wind up too under-used, uneven pacing, blocky infodumps, awkward and jarring switches out of the third-person-limited POV. Even on a sentence level it felt in need of editing: there were far too many "Clariel felt x because y" type lines, which with another pass could have been smoothed out into something much less amateur. Top that off with the fact that the book ends before the most interesting and novel part of Clariel's story and well, this wasn't at all what I've been waiting for. It felt like Nix had been writing himself back into the Old Kingdom as an exercise (he's not written in it for 10 years, after all) and somehow that freewrite got bound and published.<br /><br />The thing that makes this all the more frustrating is that there is a <i>lot</i> of potential here. Clariel herself holds most of it: she's a berserker, she's got an aptitude for necromancy, and we all know she's destined to be Chlorr of the Mask in Lirael/Abhorsen - her story could be either a fascinating story of villainous descent or a tragedy of losing a sense of self, or both. (Also, she's canonically asexual and aromantic, which makes her dear to me in particular.) Then there's the world - we've actually never seen a fully functional Old Kingdom; even in Lirael and Abhorsen it's still being rebuilt, and in Sabriel it's the nation-wide equivalent of a ghost town. Nix had a distinct opportunity here to explore what an entire country filled with necromancers, Clayr, and Charter Mages would look like... and he wrote pretty much all three of those groups out of it. The only necromancers we see are the Abhorsens, none of whom actually go into Death (not even ONE antagonistic necromancer? anywhere?); the Clayr don't really show up at all, and Charter Magic is out of fashion in the society, so doesn't play a part. (furthermore, Clariel doesn't have a strong aptitude for the Charter, so even though she's supposedly learning it the reader never really gets to see it used.) Ancelstierre plays no role in this story at all, which is... understandable but regrettable. The land beyond the Rift has the <i>potential</i> to be involved, but isn't. All this leaves the Old Kingdom feeling a great deal more generic than it does in the original trilogy, and instead of the sense of coming back to a fantasy world I loved, I wound up with the sense that a bait-and-switch had been performed.<br /><br />I wanted to enjoy this book, really I did - but all the things that I enjoyed about the original trilogy were absent. My hopes are still up for the promised post-<i>Abhorsen</i> fifth volume, especially as it's less likely to have the 'writing onesself into the world' feeling that this did by dint of coming soon (hopefully) after <i>Clariel</i>. And hey - maybe Nix will get back into the swing of things and someday we'll get a sequel to this book, or a prequel about some of the fascinating history it mentioned (lady pirates on the Ratterlin? Mistress Ader as Abhorsen? I'd love more on both). I still want more from this world and from Nix as an author; it just happens that this didn't hit the mark at all.<br /><br />A couple of final notes/quibbles under the cut:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[- Aunt Lemmin and the princess were both criminally under-used/over-mentioned. Honestly, by the end I expected them to be the same person - since otherwise there wouldn't really be enough time to develop two and I anticipated both being involved in the end. Aaaaaand then they both wound up offscreen.<br />- The villainous plot? Really didn't have enough stakes to it at all. I mean, this is a prequel by in-world chronology, but in publication it's directly following the book that ended with BINDING ORANNIS. And all we get here is a vague background attempt to break the Charter? <i>Really?</i><br />- gotta say though, I still love the complete lack of gender roles in this world. Ladies are <i>everywhere</i> and doing <i>everything</i> and that's great.<br />- there was a brief mention Clariel almost hugging Belatiel to "let out some feeling that she had long suppressed" which really bothered me; see above re: her being really firmly defined as aro-ace. That line came off as a half-assed retraction of that orientation, and felt a little like a betrayal.<br />- no seriously I want to know what's beyond the Rift NIX SEQUEL PLEASE <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="17011492840897507806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_978519908" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/978519908" />
    <a title="anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7770622-anna"><img alt="anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354917733p2/7770622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/978519908?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="anna" href="/user/show/7770622-anna">anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758627" href="/book/show/7489530-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer978519908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11193074644472971740">Received an ARC of the book. Currently about 1/4 of the way through...initial thoughts: this book is suffering from the same thing that made me dislike <i>Lirael</i>--lack of action, too much build up.<br/><br/><i>Sabriel</i> worked out so well because the beginning was quite fast paced. Problem arises, Sabriel makes the decision to do something about it and she's off to the races. I can't stand it when the protag is sort of wishy washy about going for his/her goals. I know situations change as more information is reve</span>
  <span id="freeText11193074644472971740" style="display:none">Received an ARC of the book. Currently about 1/4 of the way through...initial thoughts: this book is suffering from the same thing that made me dislike <i>Lirael</i>--lack of action, too much build up.<br /><br /><i>Sabriel</i> worked out so well because the beginning was quite fast paced. Problem arises, Sabriel makes the decision to do something about it and she's off to the races. I can't stand it when the protag is sort of wishy washy about going for his/her goals. I know situations change as more information is revealed, but at least initially I wanted Clariel to be very clear about what she wanted and how she was going to get it. If she can't even come up with some feasible plans, then she must not want her goal badly enough and I don't have the patience to read her mopey inner dialogue.<br /><br />Will continue update.<br /><br />UPDATE: Finished book 7/1/14. The book gets three stars for interesting world building. I liked finding out more about the history of the Old Kingdom, the society of Belisaere, how Free Magic can be used and the agenda of Free Magic creatures. But if you didn't like <i>Lirael</i> very much (as I didn't), then you won't like <i>Clariel</i> for probably the same reasons. Most of the book is Clariel going "wah wah I just wanna do my own thing, leave me alone" and nothing really happens until the last 3 chapters. I get the feeling that Clariel is supposed to be a tragic, tortured hero, but mostly I'm just irritated with her.<br /><br />Spoilers ahead, keep reading at your own risk.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So Clariel is pretty much the opposite of Lirael - while Lirael just wants to belong, Clariel just wants to gtfo. And that's fine. She doesn't want to be trapped, she wants to run wild and free and be alone, I get that. But Clariel just seems kind of dumb and selfish with a one-track mind. All she ever thinks about it running away--then fucking do it already. Afraid your parents will drag you back? Pull some shit until they realize you're serious, don't just throw tantrums. Life is full of people telling you what you should do, but until you get smart and learn how to play the game, you'll never be able to get out and do what you want. Just thinking you want to run and acting oh so rebellious while coming up with half baked plans won't get you anywhere. I guess I prefer my protagonists smarter and more devious? Clariel is just not a very good protagonist - she seems set up to be a support character.<br /><br />And tbh, outside of Kilp (and maybe Bel) everyone in this book was kind of dumb. They're all stubbornly refusing to do what they are supposed to do for no real reason at all. It's very frustrating. I can understand one or two people who are all "no, I just want to do what I want" but all of them? And in the end I feel like no one has really learned a lesson from all this. If you ONLY do what you want, bad people take advantage, people (like your loved ones) suffer and die. But no one seems to have figured this out (except maybe Bel). <br /><br />The unrequited love of Bel also bugged me. What exactly about Clariel made him fall in love with her? In the time they've known each other, she wasn't exactly all that friendly to him anyway. And Clariel even says that Denima is smarter and prettier - Bel disagreed, but he shouldn't have because it's true. (Well I don't know about prettier, but Denima is definitely smarter.) Either way, I could have done without Bel being all googly over Clariel. They could have just been friends the entire time. (Plus it's because of Bel's tender feelings that Clariel ends up becoming Chlorr. I'm sure if she'd been executed as planned, she would have simply died and gone on. But Bel lets her escape and she turns into Chlorr. Oops. Good job escaping, Clariel. 600 years down the line you end up becoming a slave to Free Magic.)<br /><br />This book could have done a lot better with more action straight off. Instead of all this build up, with all these people LITERALLY not doing anything (the king who won't rule, the Abhorsens who won't fight, the girl who can't figure out how to run), I wanted more palace intrigue. I wanted more weird old magic. I wanted to see the Clayr go to war. I wanted Clariel to figure out that she was being a dumb stubborn child, to grow up and take responsibility for her actions, which would have made her turning into Chlorr a truly tragic end instead of just something that happens, nbd. (Can you imagine if Clariel had turned into a true heroine and was filled with hope for herself and her friends at the end? And knowing that somehow, she would end up Chlorr and meet a terrible end...that would have been heart wrenching. But instead I'm just irritated with Clariel so I don't really care. Bah.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="11193074644472971740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1092793794?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1761880-ashley">Ashley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1092793794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer143093689285530551">I hate to give this one star because I really love Garth Nix and the Abhorsen books, but there were so many things I didn't like about this book. <br/>1) Clariel. Wow. I don't think I have ever disliked a heroine more. So selfish, so self-absorbed, and just not interesting at all. No one cares about your stupid forest, move on.<br/>2) What was this book supposed to be? Weird YA finishing school book? fantasy? All I know is almost all of it was dull. Reading about the guild outfits and the clothes in gener</span>
  <span id="freeText143093689285530551" style="display:none">I hate to give this one star because I really love Garth Nix and the Abhorsen books, but there were so many things I didn't like about this book. <br />1) Clariel. Wow. I don't think I have ever disliked a heroine more. So selfish, so self-absorbed, and just not interesting at all. No one cares about your stupid forest, move on.<br />2) What was this book supposed to be? Weird YA finishing school book? fantasy? All I know is almost all of it was dull. Reading about the guild outfits and the clothes in general was dull, the town was dull, the characters were almost all unappealing. So little happened and having to listen to Clariel complain about wanting to go to the forest what felt like every second page was just awful. The other books in the series had instantly sucked me in with their world building with the dead, bells,etc but this had none of that.<br />3) The tone of the book was off for me. People not caring about charter magic, everyone uninterested in their duties...the guilds. It just didn't work for me and I wasn't able to get excited about any of it. It also seemed so unbelievable that everyone would suck so hard. Like basically no adult character in the book was good at their job or cared about their job unless they were crazy/evil/power-hungry, etc.<br /><br />Reading this did make me decide to re-read the other Abhorsen books and I still enjoy a lot of Garth Nix's other work (Key to the Kingdom series, Confusion of Princes,etc) but I really really disliked Clariel unfortunately.</span>

<div id="review_1083326493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083326493" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16281235-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083326493?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/16281235-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083326493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12686951515543264564">Much like the Legend of Korra, this long-awaited sequel follows the ostensibly dramatic and exciting adventure of an uncharismatic and constantly whining main character in a setting that is nostalgic until you realize its rather whiny as well. Wonder how a setting can be whiny? Supporting characters fade into the background, until you look around and wonder "is this inn haunted by a complaining ghost or what?". <br/><br/><br/>The story somehow fails to convey the sense of urgency and humor that characterized t</span>
  <span id="freeText12686951515543264564" style="display:none">Much like the Legend of Korra, this long-awaited sequel follows the ostensibly dramatic and exciting adventure of an uncharismatic and constantly whining main character in a setting that is nostalgic until you realize its rather whiny as well. Wonder how a setting can be whiny? Supporting characters fade into the background, until you look around and wonder "is this inn haunted by a complaining ghost or what?". <br /><br /><br />The story somehow fails to convey the sense of urgency and humor that characterized the previous installments of the series, and is only kept alive (alive being a rather generous description, think more semi-vegetative and on life-support) by cameos by characters from the other stories (I'm looking at you Mogget). Nix makes an effort to do so, but doesn't manage to reconcile the Old Kingdom in its prime (well, not prime but much better than the crumbling wreck it was in the original trilogy) with the story itself.<br /><br />Oh yeah, and the book was far too short. I mean, it's like 300 pages, but nothing ACTUALLY HAPPENED.<br /><br />I know I'm older now, but I reread the goddamn series a couple lonths ago and it felt a lot better than this so its not childhood nostalgia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12686951515543264564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

People keep running around and being like, ‘marriage! dating! these are the most important things!’ and instead, she’s, ‘how do you have time for this; people are trying to kill us!’ and also, 'my career is far more important to me than any possibility of </span>
  <span id="freeText996980878202881692" style="display:none">Garth Nix wrote a new Abhorsen book! And not only that, there’s going to be yet another new Abhorsen book after this one! How exciting is that?<br /><br />One of the things I really liked about the book was the portrayal of the main character’s sexuality. People keep running around and being like, ‘marriage! dating! these are the most important things!’ and instead, she’s, ‘how do you have time for this; people are trying to kill us!’ and also, 'my career is far more important to me than any possibility of romance.’ I feel like these are both sensible viewpoints, and things we could see more of in YA.</span>

<div id="review_1039636879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1039636879" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6584522-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440113483p2/6584522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1039636879?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/6584522-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6584522-kat?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6584522-kat?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6584522-kat?shelf=awful-time-sucks">awful-time-sucks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1039636879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11244306494388247105">THANK GOD IT'S OVER!!!! That was one of the most painful reading experiences I have had in a long time. I honestly have not idea why the author felt this book needed to exist.<br/><br/>It really didn't.<br/><br/>Now, it was a long time ago that I read the Old Kingdom trilogy, but I am vaguely aware of liking it, if I can't quite remember the details. For example I have no idea who Clariel is supposed to become in the original series. Her name is mentioned at the end of the book, and it rings a bell, but considering</span>
  <span id="freeText11244306494388247105" style="display:none">THANK GOD IT'S OVER!!!! That was one of the most painful reading experiences I have had in a long time. I honestly have not idea why the author felt this book needed to exist.<br /><br />It really didn't.<br /><br />Now, it was a long time ago that I read the Old Kingdom trilogy, but I am vaguely aware of liking it, if I can't quite remember the details. For example I have no idea who Clariel is supposed to become in the original series. Her name is mentioned at the end of the book, and it rings a bell, but considering how utterly dull her story is, I really don't get why we needed to know about it. Don't get me wrong, some stuff happens, but the way its told, the story is left feeling plodding and bland. In fact bland is a very good word to describe most aspects of this book.<br /><br />Story? Bland<br />Writing? Bland<br />Characters? Insufferably, painfully bland.<br /><br />The characters though. Jeez, they were literally all the exact same. They spoke the same, acted the same (yup you guessed it, bland). There was no variation in their personalities. If we weren't supposed to like Clariel, then Mr Nix, you did a brilliant job. She is, quite possibly the hardest character to warm up to. She's cold, distant, selfish, and not in a cool, bad guy way which actually makes you like them. She was just plain unlikeable. Every few sentences she'd whine about how she wanted to get back to her precious forest. She had the emotional range of lard and was more than willing to abandon someone who had been trying to help her in the middle of nowhere, just so she could return to her precious forest. But like I said, maybe we're not supposed to like her. But the while point in visiting the back story of a bad guy, is to see why it is they become the people they become and possibly understand them a little better. See a different side to their personalities. All I gleaned from this book is the Clariel had no personality.<br /><br />This was quite simply, a story that lacked any kind of life, or substance. Which saddens me immensely!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11244306494388247105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1128943080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1128943080" />
    <a title="Eric Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen"><img alt="Eric Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560117879p2/6229358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1128943080?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Allen" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen">Eric Allen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1128943080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9704920107930876120">I loved the first two books in the series during high school, and I believe Abhorsen came out when I was in college, but ask any woman on earth and she'll tell you that men never really grow up, so there you go. It's been a long, long, loooooooong wait for more stories that take place in this world, and I'm excited to see that Garth Nix has more plans for it in the future.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, Clariel was a little disappointing to me. The other books are just so good, and this one, while not exactly ba</span>
  <span id="freeText9704920107930876120" style="display:none">I loved the first two books in the series during high school, and I believe Abhorsen came out when I was in college, but ask any woman on earth and she'll tell you that men never really grow up, so there you go. It's been a long, long, loooooooong wait for more stories that take place in this world, and I'm excited to see that Garth Nix has more plans for it in the future.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Clariel was a little disappointing to me. The other books are just so good, and this one, while not exactly bad, doesn't really live up to its predecessors. Most of the reason that this book was rather mediocre was because of its protagonist. Clariel is just so unlikeable that it's hard to be invested in any story about her. All she does is whine and cry about wanting to go to the forest and live her life alone away from anyone that can bother her. She hits this one-note of personality about five billion times over the course of the book.<br /><br />When you look at the other books in the series, you've got Sabriel who is a reluctant heroine drawn into a desperate fight against a monster that seeks to utterly destroy her homeland when she sets off to rescue her father. And then you've got Lirael, the outcast who finds and develops unexpected talents and abilities that lead her to a destiny far greater than anything she ever dreamed of as a child. Next to them, Clariel is rather bland, boring, and annoying. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I understand that you're really not supposed to like the character, because she does end up becoming a pretty nasty villain later on in the series. But here's the thing, even though she's going to turn into a monster LATER, she's not one NOW. If the story is going to be about her, she needs to be likeable and sympathetic, and she's not. She a whining little crybaby that does nothing but run away from her problems and never really faces any of them. The conflict at the end was of her own making, and had she just stayed put, everything would have turned out all right. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> When you don't like or don't care about the characters in a story, it's very hard to feel any of the tension and drama. Those things come from caring about the characters and genuinely wanting to see them triumph in the end. I didn't really care about Clariel throughout most of the book. I found her annoying and childish, and spent most of my time with the book wishing I was reading about Lirael (by far my favorite character in the series) instead.<br /><br />It's not a bad book, but it is a mediocre one, made more so when it is compared to Sabriel, Lirael, and Abhorsen, the previous three releases in this series. If you really want to know the origins of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Chlorr of the Mask <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> give it a try. Otherwise, this is pretty much a story that didn't really need to be told. I was hoping for a bigger look at the past of The Old Kingdom, as this book takes place 600 years before Sabriel, but everything is from Clariel's point of view, and Clariel doesn't give a crap about anything but running away to her forest, so that's the only part of The Old Kingdom's past you really get to hear much of. Though not entirely bad, it just didn't live up to my expectations for this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9704920107930876120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_344790804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344790804" />
    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344790804?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gergana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gergana" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana">Gergana</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062216809" href="/book/show/20602969-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=first-book-was-better">first-book-was-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344790804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5398252605437472006"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422896540i/13560377.jpg' height='270' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>IF I hear one more word about Clariel's stupid forest, I am buying a chainsaw ^_^ </b><br/><br/>Ok, so with THIS out of the way, I can safely say - I enjoyed <i>Clariel</i>. But ...it didn't feel like a part of the <i>Old Kingdom</i> series. In fact, it felt more like a pretty good YA novel, with an angsty teen trying to fit in the world while being misunderstood and hindered by the ignorant, unreliable adults.<br/><br/>The first 25% were absolutely amazing and filled with so much potential! The setting was interesting, the world bu</span>
  <span id="freeText5398252605437472006" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422896540i/13560377.jpg" height="270" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>IF I hear one more word about Clariel's stupid forest, I am buying a chainsaw ^_^ </b><br><br>Ok, so with THIS out of the way, I can safely say - I enjoyed <i>Clariel</i>. But ...it didn't feel like a part of the <i>Old Kingdom</i> series. In fact, it felt more like a pretty good YA novel, with an angsty teen trying to fit in the world while being misunderstood and hindered by the ignorant, unreliable adults.<br><br>The first 25% were absolutely amazing and filled with so much potential! The setting was interesting, the world building was even better than <i>Sabriel</i>'s, in my opinion, and the protagonist, Clariel, starts of as a narrow-minded, self-obsessed, unambitious 17 year old who is forced to conform to the will of her rich parents and <b>GET A LIFE</b>! So many possibilities for character development, right? ...right?<br><br>Around the middle, things get serious and there's plenty of action and pure awesomeness from Clariel and the supporting cast! You are reading about something mundane and then - SLAP! Blood, gore and heads flying around! I could not see them coming!<br><br>In addition, I give Garth Nix two thumbs up for making Clariel an A-sexual - great to see different sexual orientations depicted in fiction! Plus if Clariel whined about boyfriends as much as her forest I would've ...stopped reading...<br><br>And this is where the main problem is. <br>- Clariel wants to leave everything behind and go live in the Great <b>Forest</b>. <br>- Clariel wants to go to the <b>Forest</b><br>- Clariel wants to be a hunter and move to the <b>Forest</b><br>- Clariel hates the city and wants to be alone in the <b>Forest</b><br>- She can finally be happy if she can go to the <b>Forest</b><br>- Why can't she be in the <b>Forest</b>?<br>- blah-blah-blah <b>Forest</b><br>- blah-blah-blah <b>Forest</b><br>- etc. <b>Forest</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422896540i/13560378._SX540_.jpg" height="170" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, I am not kidding. We hear her complaining about her forest non-stop...until the very end. And that's where the second problem is - <b>Clariel never changes</b>. At one point in the book she goes through hell, she is taken away from everything she has ever known and after all this, she is still exactly the same - stubborn and ignorant. She doesn't care about anyone, she doesn't care about her friends, her family, her kingdom, the people...all she cares about is her <b>forest</b>. <br><br>Her city is in turmoil and everyone might die?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422896540i/13560379._SX540_.png" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380947170ra/3465951.gif" height="170" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Basically, she is selfish to the point where she is willing to endanger the life of her friends in order to go fulfill her personal vendetta or go to the Great <b>forest</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ You do NOT leave a wounded, exhausted friend, who has just risked his life to save you, in an unknown forest, you do NOT steal his sword and money while he's sleeping in a place where wild animals are obviously lurking around, you do NOT even consider doing this! It's wrong to even think about it!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The ending, alas, felt rushed and unsatisfying (in my own opinion). After the intense fights in the middle, nothing much happens up to around 95% and even then, you keep wondering what Clariel is thinking (apart from the <b>forest</b>, of course)<br><br>...I know I sound negative, but the truth is I could not put this book down. Despite all my problems with the main character, the story was thrilling and it manages to keep you on your toes most of the time!<br><br>I definitely recommend to check <i>Clariel</i> out if you:<br>-are a fan of Garth Nix's <i>Old Kingdom</i> series.<br>-enjoy angsty YA novels<br>-don't mind repetitions<br>-are passionate about the <b>forest</b><br><br>Enjoy! <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5398252605437472006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1249721843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249721843" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249721843?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=children-s-and-ya">children-s-and-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249721843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16347768542928781371">It’s a bit surprising to me to see the disappointed reviews of this, because I quite enjoyed it. Of course, it’s a different world to the one Sabriel enters, and different even from the world that Lirael and Sameth have to navigate as Sabriel and Touchstone work on restoring the Old Kingdom. This one doesn’t feature any contact with Ancelstierre, and is set before even Touchstone/Torrigan’s time. So naturally, the concerns of its people, the politics, are all quite different. It’s interesting to</span>
  <span id="freeText16347768542928781371" style="display:none">It’s a bit surprising to me to see the disappointed reviews of this, because I quite enjoyed it. Of course, it’s a different world to the one Sabriel enters, and different even from the world that Lirael and Sameth have to navigate as Sabriel and Touchstone work on restoring the Old Kingdom. This one doesn’t feature any contact with Ancelstierre, and is set before even Touchstone/Torrigan’s time. So naturally, the concerns of its people, the politics, are all quite different. It’s interesting to see an Abhorsen clan which is much larger than that of Sabriel’s time, but which is decidedly weaker; it’s interesting to see in Sameth the diffidence of earlier Abhorsens.<br /><br />But in fact, I like Clariel herself rather more than Lirael or Sameth. She has goals and she pursues them, and she doesn’t have to take on responsibility, but she does. Of course, all her choices go wrong, unlike Sabriel or Lirael’s. If you think about the guiding words of these books, “Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?” — you could almost say that Sabriel, knowing her choices, chooses her path. Clariel’s path chooses her, because she’s not given the information she needs to make her own choice. In neither case is there really an alternate way, but Sabriel’s path is knowing and Clariel’s is forced.<br /><br />It’s interesting to get a look at the bloodlines in the land and how they work out in a time of peace. Because of the strength of Sabriel and her father, and Touchstone and Sabriel’s rule, it’s easy in the trilogy to think that when the bloodlines are in the right place, everything will be alright. Clariel shows us that it isn’t, and gives us a picture of the other troubles of the Old Kingdom. There are no Dead creatures here in this book; instead we see the Abhorsens and Charter mages needing to deal with the other threat, of Free Magic.<br /><br />One thing I really loved, on a character-level, is that Clariel is explicitly asexual. She’s not interested, she’s not going to change her mind for the right person or something, and like many ace people, she’s even experimented a bit to try and figure out how that all works. It’s awesome that she doesn’t really have conflict about this, and while people think she may be mistaken, nobody’s pushing her to “fix” it, or guilting her because she doesn’t want that.<br /><br />In a way, the story feels very incomplete, because it’s just a fragment of a life, a tiny piece of the history of the Old Kingdom, and it doesn’t connect up the dots between this book and the original trilogy. There is plenty of room for many, many more stories, even ones featuring the same characters, should Nix choose. But we do have the shape of Clariel’s life sketched out for us, between this book and the original trilogy; I think it may be more satisfying seen that way, rather than read as a stand-alone.<br /><br /><a href="http://breathesbooks.com/2015/09/16/review-clariel/" rel="nofollow noopener">Originally posted here.</a> Some discussion in the comments!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16347768542928781371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_907775391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907775391" />
    <a title="Josh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1108056-josh"><img alt="Josh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306470229p2/1108056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907775391?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josh" href="/user/show/1108056-josh">Josh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758627" href="/book/show/7489530-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=read_2014">read_2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1108056-josh?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907775391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4991770260738483752">I've been waiting for another novel set in the world of the Old Kingdom for a long time now, and, despite having moments that brought back the enjoyment of LIRAEL and SABRIEL, the long ago prequel to SABRIEL doesn't quite live up to my expectations.<br/><br/>CLARIEL leans heavily towards the YA styling's of Garth Nix's other fantasy series targeted at that demographic. The toned down storytelling is evident, as is the teenage angst and constant reference to love despite Clariel's predicament (even though </span>
  <span id="freeText4991770260738483752" style="display:none">I've been waiting for another novel set in the world of the Old Kingdom for a long time now, and, despite having moments that brought back the enjoyment of LIRAEL and SABRIEL, the long ago prequel to SABRIEL doesn't quite live up to my expectations.<br /><br />CLARIEL leans heavily towards the YA styling's of Garth Nix's other fantasy series targeted at that demographic. The toned down storytelling is evident, as is the teenage angst and constant reference to love despite Clariel's predicament (even though she shows no interest in her male suitors, it's a constant theme throughout).<br /><br />Clariel, sees her family decimated before her eyes, traverses the Old Kingdom in search of the Abhorsens for sanctuary from the threat of the Belisaere governor. Here, readers of the series are treated with a familiar character and further elements of Free Magic as Clariel slowly builds towards realizing her path and takes the first tentative steps towards justice for her slain family. <br /><br />I really liked the last third of CLARIE. It had everything I'd come to love from the Old Kingdom trilogy before it (mages, free and charter magic, bells), yet the set up is what let CLARIEL down. <br /><br />My rating: 3/5 stars. <br /><br />Review first appeared on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://justaguywholikes2read.blogspot.com.au/2014/10/review-clariel-by-garth-nix.html">http://justaguywholikes2read.blogspot...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4991770260738483752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_965052008" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965052008" />
    <a title="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library"><img alt="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560136145p2/11289146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965052008?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" href="/user/show/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library">Nemo (The Moonlight Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=sts">sts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer965052008&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965052008" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10472493437592614146">SUMMARY<br/>Clariel is better known as the centuries-old necromancer and later the Greater Dead creature Chlorr of the Mask in Lirael. This is her early story.<br/><br/>PLOT<br/>Clariel wants nothing more than to live as a Borderer in the Great Forest of Estwael. So when she is dragged by her Master Goldsmith mother Jaciel to Belisaire, to marry the Governer’s son Aronzo and forever be trapped in a life she is desperate to escape, Clariel takes steps to ensure her own freedom – even if it comes at a great cost.<br/>This</span>
  <span id="freeText10472493437592614146" style="display:none">SUMMARY<br />Clariel is better known as the centuries-old necromancer and later the Greater Dead creature Chlorr of the Mask in Lirael. This is her early story.<br /><br />PLOT<br />Clariel wants nothing more than to live as a Borderer in the Great Forest of Estwael. So when she is dragged by her Master Goldsmith mother Jaciel to Belisaire, to marry the Governer’s son Aronzo and forever be trapped in a life she is desperate to escape, Clariel takes steps to ensure her own freedom – even if it comes at a great cost.<br />This is not your typical origin story. This does not detail how Clariel becomes Chlorr the necromancer – rather, it details the early steps taken by Clariel so that you can understand how someone from the ‘good’ side of magic can become so twisted and corrupted. Clariel is not gifted with strong Charter Magic nor much knowledge of the Abhorsens due to a family feud, but she is gifted with the beserk rage familiar in both Touchstone and Sam, and that is tainted with Free Magic. Through the Free Magic, Clariel works to get what she wants – but doing the wrong thing for the right reason is still the wrong thing, and that’s a lesson I Clariel doesn’t learn, and I suspect still doesn’t learn later in her life and contributes to her downfall as Chlorr.<br /><br />CHARACTERS<br />Clariel is of course our protagonist. She’s strong-willed and knows exactly what she wants in life, even at only 17. She’s also trapped under her mother’s tyrannical reign. It’s super easy to identify with Clariel’s chafing need to spread her wings and be independent, knowing she will thrive in her chosen career as a Borderer, and feel the helpless obedience that comes with being a dependent child. She’s also asexual, which I think, for some, might be interesting. I couldn’t really tell if it was just used as a minor plot point to keep rejecting certain suitors’ advancements on her. It certainly was easy to feel her horror as news of her arranged marriage came through. She’s not particularly selfish but she is self-absorbed to the point where that’ll the catalyst, she’s abrasive to the horror of other characters and doesn’t want to take part in their charades.<br />We see little of Clariel’s parents, her father who does the admin side of the goldsmithing business despite being a talented smith himself, and Jaciel, who is more obsessed with her work than he own family.<br />Also appearing is the Abhorsen-in-Waiting-in-Waiting, Belariel, or Bel, who is Clariel’s cousin and friend from the Academy. Bel is concerned that the current Abhorsens, in a family of 300 strong, are too busy ceremoniously hunting to face the tasks required of the real Abhosren, so Bel’s been training at night and reading The Book of the Dead in secret.<br />Also popping up for a pretty major role in corrupting Clariel is Moggett, the wiley twisty little feline-bound Free Magic creature who cannot be trusted!<br /><br />WRITING<br />The biggest issue I had going in was that I was expecting more of clean and cut origin story when really, it sort of hinted at Clariel’s weakness and her eventual downfall to come. Imagine writing a Joker origin story where at the end he’s just getting involved in crime but he doesn’t fall into the vat of chemicals that changes him forever; or a Batman Begins without Bruce Wayne ever making the Batsuit; or a Superman story that is basically Smallville where we never see Supes don the cape, but while that works for Smallville, it took me until actually finishing the book to realise I wasn’t going to get Clariel’s tragic fall into the Joker vat of chemicals after all. We don’t see her become a necromancer – we see her fight the urge. We don’t see her do anything evil, really – she still tries to save lives and even though she does murder people, that can be viewed through a justice or revenge lens.<br /><br />PACING<br />This book tricks you. It tricks you into thinking it’s got a slower pace than it does. We follow Clariel around the city for the first third before anything of interest really happens, much like following Lirael in the library – it’s all a big set up that you don’t even realise is happening. Then it’s all go-go-go all the time until you’re screaming at yourself to stop reading so fast, it’ll all be over soon.<br /><br />OVERALL<br />I certainly think Clariel is a book you’ll only get the most enjoyment out of if you’ve read the previous Old Kingdom books.<br /><br />I received this book for free from Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10472493437592614146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14305902573535102412" style="display:none">I was lucky enough to get a ARC of this at BEA in New York and let me tell you it was worth the ten years of waiting. I can't get kids at my school to read the series, or if they do they don't tell me about it, but they are nuts is all I can say because this stuff is so good it makes my head hurt. I look into the air as I read this and look for Charter Marks. None yet but I am not giving up hope!<br /><br />The story took some time to build but now I am bereft that it is over. I was hoping for more magic early on but once it rolled it rolled right over me!<br /><br />And I would have said any time with Mogget is a good time but he was on fire this time. I really got a good feel for the Free Magic that lies just underneath that collar of his.<br /><br />And the note at the end? Drove me right back to the older books in the series!<br /><br />Worth the wait but now I have to decide if I go right back to read the other books or if I tear myself away from the Old Kingdom just so that I don't drive my family crazy ringing bells! What I would give for a set of bells!!!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susana" href="/user/show/7301000-susana">Susana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=tstlc">tstlc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=series-gone-sour">series-gone-sour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=series-i-ve-given-up">series-i-ve-given-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=not-my-cup-of-tea">not-my-cup-of-tea</a>,
