          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer734240431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6253581058426494321">2.5 stars<br/><br/><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/> <b>Arc provided by Harper Collins through Edelweiss</b><br/><br/>It was my intention to re-read the previous books of this "Old Kingdom" series, before picking this one up.<br/>Unfortunately I wasn't able to find the necessary time to do it, and I only got to read about half of the first book, Sabriel, before starting with this one.<br/><br/> And although I do still like Sabriel, I am afraid that time seems to have diluted my love for this series. :/<br/>The writing never seemed to "flow"...<br/><br/>I read Sabriel for the firs</span>
  <span id="freeText6253581058426494321" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br><br><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br> <b>Arc provided by Harper Collins through Edelweiss</b><br><br>It was my intention to re-read the previous books of this "Old Kingdom" series, before picking this one up.<br>Unfortunately I wasn't able to find the necessary time to do it, and I only got to read about half of the first book, Sabriel, before starting with this one.<br><br> And although I do still like Sabriel, I am afraid that time seems to have diluted my love for this series. :/<br>The writing never seemed to "flow"...<br><br>I read Sabriel for the first time ever, almost twelve years ago, and I loved it!<br>But many reads have come and gone since then, and I am afraid that my memory was being kinder compared to the actual reality of what I read.<br><br>This is not to say that I don't like it anymore.<br>I do!<br><br>I like the world the author created, and this story helped make things a little clearer about the relationship between Abhorsen's , Free Magic elements and Mogget.<br><br>But although I may like the world in which the stories take place, this one ended up being extremely hard to read! In fact the only reason I finished it, was out of love for the series.<br><br>That, and because Mogget appears in all his sarcastic, interesting, glory!<br><br><u>This is not to say that this is a bad book...it definitely isn't!</u><br><br> The problem is that I ended up having to force myself to finish it.<br><br>The beginning was awfully slow, and the main character has you "headdesking" and "face-palming".. constantly!<br><br>Clariel is boring, uninteresting, basically a disaster waiting to happen, and she spends the majority of the story constantly saying how much she wants to go and live by herself in the Great Forest!<br><u>I am not exaggerating, she's constantly whining about it.</u><br><br>Look at the book cover: Do you see what is written there?<br><br> <b>
  <i>A passion thwarted will often go astray</i>
</b><br><br>Her passion is to live alone in the Great Forest...so when life leads her to another path, she manages to f**** up in a colossal scale! (sorry, but I can't remember another word to describe the level of idiot moves she makes!)<br><br>In fact she could be nominated for the <i>"most stupid character ever created"</i> in the 2014 book awards.<br><br>So, it doesn't come as a surprise what her future turns out to be, does it?<br>Do I care than she turns out to be the big bad villain, in the previously published books?<br>No.<br><br>Does it surprise me?<br>*snort*<br><br>A thing that I can't help mention, is that the author takes great pains in developing an asexual character.<br><br>We are told that Clariel has had sexual relations in the past, but that in the end she didn't found herself particularly interested in the thing, lol, and that she also isn't interested in women....<br>*sigh*<br>*deep breath*<br>Who cares?<br><br> I am just reading this for the plot, and although these stories have what you can consider ya characters, I never found these stories ya per se...so comments like these just end up being superfluous to the story.<br><br>We all know that it is possible to read an interesting book without said book having to had a romance in it!<br><br>I don't know, this made me remember a comment that Sabriel makes in her own book, when she says that she's not interested in Touchstone in that way, and that sex is a complication and blah, blah...and I was like: <br><br><i>But why would the author feel the need to say this?</i><br><br>I hadn't felt anything going on between them in the first place! She only kissed him because the guy was made out of wood _literally _ and she was trying to break the spell!!<br><br>Ah....long story....and back to Clariel...<br><br>Garth Nix should really skip these <i>"out of the blue"</i> romances: In this one there's a character that all of a sudden finds himself ...I don't know...attracted, in love..in lust for Clariel?<br><br>Which ended up being pretty much pathetic, because once again it comes out from nowhere, and I just couldn't help feeling that it only existed, so that Clariel could be all: <i>Dude, I don't care about that sort of thing! I JUST WANT TO GO INTO THE GREAT FOREST ALL BY MYSELF!!</i><br>Fine girl, GO!! ~ I can't hear you anymore~<br><br>To finish this up, I also have to mention another aspect that I really found annoying:<br><br> Clariel is just unbelievably clueless about <b>everything</b>!<br><br>Of course this just creates the perfect setting for all the disasters that she is about to commit!<br><br>Like I said: One perfect disaster just waiting to happen...<br><br>Bottom Line: Ignorance is not a blessing, and ends up being very annoying to read about!<br><br>___________<br><br>Oh, and did you know that there is going to be another Abhorsen book, this one following Nicholas and Lirael story?<br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6253581058426494321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256603-sara?shelf=i-give-up">i-give-up</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635331669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7015170400800172016">Obviously its not fair to review this since I didn't finish it but I just can't take it anymore. Garth Nix's "Abhorsen" books are just wonderful. I believe I waxed rhapsodic about Tim Curry's outstanding narration of the first three books in this series that chronicle two kingdoms; the Old Kingdom where the Charter (basically a magic that connects everything in the kingdom) rules and necromancer's, free magic users, and the dead are kept in check by the Abhorsen (basically a wizard who can walk </span>
  <span id="freeText7015170400800172016" style="display:none">Obviously its not fair to review this since I didn't finish it but I just can't take it anymore. Garth Nix's "Abhorsen" books are just wonderful. I believe I waxed rhapsodic about Tim Curry's outstanding narration of the first three books in this series that chronicle two kingdoms; the Old Kingdom where the Charter (basically a magic that connects everything in the kingdom) rules and necromancer's, free magic users, and the dead are kept in check by the Abhorsen (basically a wizard who can walk in death using a special set of magical bells) and Ancelstierre where magic cannot be used that's more or less a sort of industrial age America with regular governments and armies etc. <br /><br />Nix is just an amazing world builder, his stories are deceptively simple in their construction (magic vs. 'the real world) and he might be covering old ground with his plots but the mythology and magic are absolutely first rate and wonderfully detailed. He writes strong, multi layered female leads and does it brilliantly. There's plenty of action but its balanced by deep relationships between the characters and believably organic love stories. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20662728.Clariel__Abhorsen___4_" title="Clariel (Abhorsen, #4) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Clariel</a> is intended as something of an origin story for one of the peripheral characters from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47624.Lirael__Abhorsen___2_" title="Lirael (Abhorsen, #2) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Lirael</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/334643.Abhorsen__Abhorsen___3_" title="Abhorsen (Abhorsen, #3) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Abhorsen</a> the last two books in the original trilogy. Though I normally classify origin stories somewhere between root canals and having to hang out with my husband's friend J.P. (who is the absolute WORST let me tell you) for Garth Nix I'm willing to give it a shot. Besides the character in question is a pretty cool one and I found myself actually getting into the idea of finding out how she got where she is when we meet her in the original trilogy.<br /><br />Sadly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20662728.Clariel__Abhorsen___4_" title="Clariel (Abhorsen, #4) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Clariel</a>, while still showcasing the wonderful descriptions and mythos of the earlier books is deadly, deadly dull. <br /><br />She's just not interesting guys. Like at all. <br /><br />Her story begins 600 years before the events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/518848.Sabriel__Abhorsen___1_" title="Sabriel (Abhorsen, #1) by Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Sabriel</a> when the Old Kingdom has been at peace for so long no one even really remembers what an Abhorsen does (including the Abhorsen) and the king has all but abdicated in favor of the various merchant guilds who are the real rulers. <br /><br />Clariel has been forced by her parents to move to the capital city of Belisaire where her mother, the greatest goldsmith of her generation, has been asked to join the Goldsmith's Guild. Clariel is utterly miserable. A loner by nature she longs to spend her life in the forest's of her homeland as a border guard but her parent's are determined to use her as a pawn for their own plans.<br /><br />If I never hear the words "forest" or "I want to be left alone" again it will be too soon. This is literally all Clariel thinks or talks about (for the sizable portion of the book I listened to). Every single thing she does or says is some variation on "I miss the forest", "I wish I were in the forest", and "how can I get back to the forest?"<br /><br />You don't even get to any actual story until you're ten chapters in and by that point I was too bored to care. <br /><br />So I have no idea if Clariel makes it back to her forest or if anyone started caring about Abhorsens' again (thought it obviously happened eventually hence the first three books) and alas I do not care in the slightest to find out.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7015170400800172016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_954549017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954549017" />
    <a title="Grace Troxel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6079682-grace-troxel"><img alt="Grace Troxel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523841246p2/6079682.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954549017?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace Troxel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace Troxel" href="/user/show/6079682-grace-troxel">Grace Troxel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758627" href="/book/show/7489530-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer954549017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13478679832799913052">This review originally appeared on my blog, Books Without Any Pictures:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookswithoutanypictures.com/2014/07/21/clariel-garth-nix/'>http://bookswithoutanypictures.com/20...</a><br/><br/>Disclaimer: This is a ridiculously early review.<br/><br/>When I was a teenager, I was obsessed with Garth Nix’s Abhorsen trilogy. I read and re-read Sabriel and Lirael until the paperbacks very clearly showed how much they’d been loved, and jumped for joy when Abhorsen was finally released. Nix’s stories had everything to love–undead villains, strong protagonists, sarcastic kitties, bardic weapo</span>
  <span id="freeText13478679832799913052" style="display:none">This review originally appeared on my blog, Books Without Any Pictures:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookswithoutanypictures.com/2014/07/21/clariel-garth-nix/">http://bookswithoutanypictures.com/20...</a><br /><br />Disclaimer: This is a ridiculously early review.<br /><br />When I was a teenager, I was obsessed with Garth Nix’s Abhorsen trilogy. I read and re-read Sabriel and Lirael until the paperbacks very clearly showed how much they’d been loved, and jumped for joy when Abhorsen was finally released. Nix’s stories had everything to love–undead villains, strong protagonists, sarcastic kitties, bardic weapons, and enchanted paper airplanes that you can really ride in.<br /><br />Now, almost a decade later, Garth Nix is finally releasing Clariel, a prequel novel set several hundred years in the past. Clariel‘s release date is set for October, and clearly I’m writing a ridiculously early review. I’VE BEEN WAITING TEN YEARS FOR THIS BOOK AND COULDN’T WAIT ANY LONGER!<br /><br />This review is going to be vague, brief, and spoiler-free, because I don’t want to give away too much before the book comes out. At the same time, there’s a lot of food for thought, and I’d really like to discuss it in more depth.<br /><br />Clariel starts out in a very young-adulty kind of way. Yes, the whole series is YA, but Clariel is more what I think of when I think of YA. Clariel’s mother is a goldsmith, and when she’s offered a promotion through her guild, she uproots the whole family from their home in the country and drags them to the capital city. Being a high-ranking member of society means that Clariel is expected to marry or become a goldsmith herself, but she’s having none of it. All she wants to do is go back to the forest, which is the one place where she truly feels free. But of course, life doesn’t work that way, and people don’t always get what they want. The kingdom is crumbling because the king refuses to lead, the Abhorsen stops banishing the dead, and a free magic creature hiding in the city could be the one thing that makes the fragile peace fall apart.<br /><br />My one criticism of the book is that there’s a lot of buildup to the action that occurs at the end of the book, and for a while, I wondered if anything was going to happen.<br /><br />For the first few chapters, I felt a bit suspicious. I wasn’t sure that Clariel could live up to the previous books, or even that Clariel herself could compare to the later characters that I know and love. I was wrong. Clariel grew on me, because she’s the sort of protagonist who can both make mistakes and be heroic without being thrown into the false dichotomy of good versus evil. She’s a free spirit who’s been confined by societal expectations, and she rebels against it. Clariel makes questionable decisions, but in doing so becomes an independent force that I can’t help but like, even while knowing that the path she chooses isn’t what one would consider the “right” one.<br /><br />Oh, and did I mention that Clariel is probably asexual? You don’t see nearly enough of that in literature, period. There’s got to be a romance, and opting out never seems to be an option. It’s unusual to see a character who knows and recognizes that she isn’t interested in love or sex. She’s a loner, and she knows it. It’s awesome.<br /><br />Well done, Garth Nix. Clariel does not disappoint.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13478679832799913052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_503401944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/503401944" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/503401944?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=treasure-and-adventure">treasure-and-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=here-be-dragons">here-be-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=class-gender-race">class-gender-race</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503401944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4318983159499286900">This is a prequel, and prequels can be dicey, so let me just start by saying: this could have been much, much, much worse.<br/><br/><i>Clariel</i> is the story–not of how young Clariel becomes Chlorr of the Mask from the original series like I was expecting it to be–but of how the foundations for that eventual change are laid. Seventeen year old Clariel moves with her family to the city of Belisaere. Clariel’s a girl of the forest, so right away this makes her unhappy, but the city and the people she encounters </span>
  <span id="freeText4318983159499286900" style="display:none">This is a prequel, and prequels can be dicey, so let me just start by saying: this could have been much, much, much worse.<br /><br /><i>Clariel</i> is the story–not of how young Clariel becomes Chlorr of the Mask from the original series like I was expecting it to be–but of how the foundations for that eventual change are laid. Seventeen year old Clariel moves with her family to the city of Belisaere. Clariel’s a girl of the forest, so right away this makes her unhappy, but the city and the people she encounters are extra bizarre. For me, also. The Old Kingdom we first see in the original trilogy is one full of magic and dead things coming back to life. Sorcerers, Abhorsens and other magic users are respected and necessary. But the world Clariel encounters is messed up. Magic users are looked down upon. The Abhorsen and his family don’t take their (very important) work seriously. And something dead is wandering around the city, causing trouble.<br /><br />All Clariel wants is to move back to the forest, but the city and her teachers and her parents and her cousin the Abhorsen-in-waiting all want her to do other things. To learn magic. To read the book of the dead. To resist the temptation she begins to feel after coming into contact with a free magic being at the beginning of the novel.<br /><br />This one is tough, because Garth Nix is one of my favorite writers, and there’s not actually anything *wrong* with what he’s written in this book. It was fun to see the Old Kingdom 600 years before the original trilogy, even with it as effed up as it was. I also really liked Clariel and empathized with her, to the point where it was painful to read about her descent into free magic sorcery. But. I also feel like all the <i>really</i> interesting stuff just started happening as the book ended, so ultimately I just finished the book feeling really unbalanced by the story.<br /><br />[3.5 stars]</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143867773" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143867773" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143867773?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=sword-and-sorcery">sword-and-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143867773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18160861483705623431">2.5<br/><br/>I didn't hate this book, but considering that the original trilogy is still one of my Top 10 of all time, and how long we've been waiting for this prequel... I am all hella kinda of disappointed.<br/><br/>I feel like the biggest issue with this book is that Clariel is just so one dimensional. Well, that and the fact that kinda everyone sucks except Belatiel and Kargrin. (I kinda think the book might been better if it were written about Belatiel and Clariel stayed a secondary character, but we learned a</span>
  <span id="freeText18160861483705623431" style="display:none">2.5<br><br>I didn't hate this book, but considering that the original trilogy is still one of my Top 10 of all time, and how long we've been waiting for this prequel... I am all hella kinda of disappointed.<br><br>I feel like the biggest issue with this book is that Clariel is just so one dimensional. Well, that and the fact that kinda everyone sucks except Belatiel and Kargrin. (I kinda think the book might been better if it were written about Belatiel and Clariel stayed a secondary character, but we learned about her through his interactions with her. It's like, we still could've gotten Clariel's story, but we could've gotten more, too.)<br><br>But Clariel wants to be a Borderer in the Forest, and that's her one ambition. Her parents move her to the city for her mother's ambition, there's politics and society and the usual fish-out-of-water type stuff, and the thing is I could sympathize with Clariel in a way, because her mom was a selfish bitch and her dad was a coward and I hate the whole, "you don't know what you want, we know what's best for you shit", except Clariel comes across as whiny instead of put-upon and every other freaking page it's "I want to go back to the Forest".<br><br>And this is disappointing because one of the pluses, to me, of Sabriel and Lirael is that they were fleshed out characters. They had their issues and feelings of being put upon and even, dare I say, a bit of whininess, but they were so much better drawn and realized as characters.<br><br>Clariel never gets past this one defining trait, and it makes her rather annoying and short-sighted. <br><br>Of course, she's not the only character which suffers. Every character is pretty thinly drawn in this one, but you at least expect it a little from the secondary characters. As I said earlier, I would've liked to see more of Belatiel and the one girl who likes him (Demi-something) and Kargrin, but they're pretty sketched as characters, too.<br><br>But, anyway, things did start to pick up once the plot kicked in and it wasn't just Clariel 'wanting to go back to the Forest' constantly, but even then, after Clariel's <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[parents get killed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, she wants to leave everything up to everyone else, and the moment where I really lost any care for her was when she was going to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[leave Belatiel high and dry just so she could get back to the Forest. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Even when she finally gets motivated to do stuff, it comes across as more a petulant pique because other people aren't doing what she wants them to do as opposed to any proactive element on her part. <br><br>And, speaking of, can we just say how much of a flaming hypocrite Clariel is? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tyriel should stop being afraid of Death and be a decent Abhorsen, and the princess should stop hiding and be a Queen, but I'm just gonna run off to the fucking Forest and never mind that some asshole killed my parents. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And she's not necessarily wrong about the first two points, but it's the last which kills it.<br><br>Anyway - <br><br>It was sort of interesting to see Belisaere before it becomes a ghost town, and to see the state of the Old Kingdom in this time period. I kind of got a Rome before the Fall vibe from it - though I think this could've been explored more. I would've liked to see a bit more of the society. I mean, it's an interesting world in which magic is seen as a servant thing. Usually magic either makes people elite, or its persecuted, but it's not common for it just to be seen as too much work. (Of course, I didn't entirely grok that, either, because the aristocracy wasn't lazy and idle - they were actually the merchants and higher level workers, so I didn't really understand the mindset in the world Nix was creating.)<br><br>So there are some interesting parts to the story, and it wasn't a complete loss... <br><br>But so many people acted so stupidy, and Clariel was so annoyingly one-note, that I couldn't really get invested in the story fully, and I actually sort of wished, at the end, that they just <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[let her die <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419205899ra/13010729.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>***<br><br>So - <br><br>Luckily this hasn't had the effect of poisoning the rest of the series for me. I still adore the trilogy, and, if anything, this has made me want to reread it.<br><br>But I think I'll pretend that this book doesn't exist or, if it does, I'll just think about how Belatiel is a cool character, and how it's a pity we didn't see more of him.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18160861483705623431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Roslyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/711951-roslyn"><img alt="Roslyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278554725p2/711951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836945160?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roslyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roslyn" href="/user/show/711951-roslyn">Roslyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758627" href="/book/show/7489530-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836945160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1700265845981818636">3.5<br/><br/>It's difficult for me to rate this novel. For a start, it didn’t engage me until nearly half-way through. This is partly because this is a prequel to the other Abhorsen novels and the world we are thrust into is not what it will later become. It's also because its protagonist, Clariel, is at first a difficult character to like and engage with. Until that half-way point, the novel felt static and I could have put it down at any point. (In fact, I accidentally left it on my work desk before a w</span>
  <span id="freeText1700265845981818636" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />It's difficult for me to rate this novel. For a start, it didn’t engage me until nearly half-way through. This is partly because this is a prequel to the other Abhorsen novels and the world we are thrust into is not what it will later become. It's also because its protagonist, Clariel, is at first a difficult character to like and engage with. Until that half-way point, the novel felt static and I could have put it down at any point. (In fact, I accidentally left it on my work desk before a week-long period when I wasn’t going to be at work, and I didn’t miss it at all). However, I’m glad I persisted. Clariel gradually came to life as a conflicted, understandable character I sympathised with and ached for. <br /><br />It’s hard to say anything meaningful about Clariel, either the character or the novel, without spoilers. Very mild spoilers below, but I think if you’re intending to read this, it might be best to avoid any information about it at all.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It was precisely because I came to care about Clariel’s fate that this became a difficult read for me even as it began to engage me. Once her inner conflict and where that was leading became clear (although I did have an idea beforehand because a lot of reviews reveal the information), I began to find the novel both much more interesting but at the same time an emotionally painful read.<br /><br />Nix’s portrayal of Clariel’s transformation is skilfully executed. Every choice she makes along the way is completely believable, so that the final disintegration comes with considerable sadness and force. And the fact that her intentions had been basically good all along only make it even more poignant.<br /><br />I like the way Nix refuses to equate Free Magic with evil. The wild ferocious will to power and violence of the Free Creatures do appear evil in human terms, and of course the Charter is needed in order to contain these primal chaotic forces and make life possible. Clariel seems to realise and accept this, even at the end, but her actions have led to irreversible changes to her that align her with Free magic more than with humanity. <br /><br />There is a certain bleakness about this novel and I think I appreciated rather than enjoyed it, exactly. After what felt to me like an unspectacular beginning, Nix does an excellent job of portraying the psychological process that leads Clariel to become what she becomes.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1123216324" />
    <a title="Yzabel Ginsberg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/549584-yzabel-ginsberg"><img alt="Yzabel Ginsberg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442957782p2/549584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20761075-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/549584-yzabel-ginsberg?shelf=annoying-characters">annoying-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/549584-yzabel-ginsberg?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/549584-yzabel-ginsberg?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/549584-yzabel-ginsberg?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/549584-yzabel-ginsberg?shelf=good-ideas-but">good-ideas-but</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1123216324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17262533039825951415">Not what I expected. The Old Kingdom looked like it was fraying, but I thought this wanted for more details about why everyone was shirking their duties, hiding their Charter marks, etc. What about the lost princess? Did everyone just run away because reasons/pressure/not wanting to bother?<br/><br/>Clariel wasn't a character I could push myself to care for (too whiny, too much "I want to go back to the Forest" too often...). The first half of the book was kind of boring, and then when things started to p</span>
  <span id="freeText17262533039825951415" style="display:none">Not what I expected. The Old Kingdom looked like it was fraying, but I thought this wanted for more details about why everyone was shirking their duties, hiding their Charter marks, etc. What about the lost princess? Did everyone just run away because reasons/pressure/not wanting to bother?<br /><br />Clariel wasn't a character I could push myself to care for (too whiny, too much "I want to go back to the Forest" too often...). The first half of the book was kind of boring, and then when things started to pick up, Clariel still seemed like she wanted revenge for something that she didn't feel <i>that</i> strongly about (still going on about "when this is over, I can finally go to the Forest", yadda-yadda). Also, the vague romance bit was, IMHO, plucked out of nowhere. It didn't bring anything to the story, and there wasn't even any particular reason for it to happen.<br /><br />The ending left me feel wanting for more, considering who Clariel was fated to become. It would have been more interesting for me if it had ended on a clearer note in the latter regard. It could've been so much more...<br /><br />1.5 stars, rounded to 2 because no matter what, I still like the Old Kingdom world.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_981443759" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/981443759" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20146142-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367982725p2/20146142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/981443759?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/20146142-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741758627" href="/book/show/7489530-clariel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20146142-maria?shelf=galleys">galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20146142-maria?shelf=to-read-again">to-read-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer981443759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4156609290373613235">Maybe I was in a bad mood. Maybe I read it too fast. Maybe I don't remember the Abhorsen trilogy well enough. Maybe, being no longer teenaged, I no longer resonate the same way with teenaged protagonists. Maybe time and nostalgia have rendered those books flawless in my heart, and nothing could stack up. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Maybe not knowing before-hand that this is the story of Chlorr of the Mask robbed me of some essential perspective. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Maybe it breaks my heart, but my feelings are </span>
  <span id="freeText4156609290373613235" style="display:none">Maybe I was in a bad mood. Maybe I read it too fast. Maybe I don't remember the Abhorsen trilogy well enough. Maybe, being no longer teenaged, I no longer resonate the same way with teenaged protagonists. Maybe time and nostalgia have rendered those books flawless in my heart, and nothing could stack up. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Maybe not knowing before-hand that this is the story of Chlorr of the Mask robbed me of some essential perspective. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Maybe it breaks my heart, but my feelings are hovering between "liked it" and "it was ok," certainly not "loved it."<br /><br />As I mentioned, I couldn't resonate with Clariel in the same way that I did with Lirael, or to a lesser extent Sabriel. She seemed to have one dimension, namely, "but I don't WANT TO" <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and so her desire for revenge at the end of the book feels shoe-horned in, rather than a natural development for a hurting character. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She's a "strong female character," but as far as I can tell, only in that she has a strong aversion to anything feminine. <br /><br />I found myself much more interested in the secondary, even tertiary characters. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The Mistress of the Academy, the Tea Teacher, Jaciel the goldsmith, and especially Bel the hapless Abhorsen <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> All far more compelling than Clariel herself.<br /><br />Maybe this is because of the aforementioned mood, but I also had trouble visualizing a few locations in the book, like Nix's descriptions were rich, but ineffective. Just how big is Kargren's tower, anyway? And the Islet?<br /><br />That said, it was still an exciting story, and I couldn't put it down. Anyway, because this is an Old Kingdom novel, and the world is still that strange, beautiful combination of order and chaos, and because this is only a galley, after all, I am not willing to write it off yet.<br /><br />In time, I will re-read the trilogy, followed by this. With that context, I may find a new appreciation for Clariel. Or maybe not.<br /><br />In the end, I guess while it doesn't hold a candle to the other stories, it's still worth a read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4156609290373613235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10068760088965104134">1. Sabriel ★★★ 1/2 <br/>2. Lirael ★★★★<br/>3. Abhorsen ★★★★<br/>4. Clariel ★★★<br/><br/>I'm not too sure how I feel about this one. I loved Clariel. She was a bad ass heroine. She didnt take shit from anyone. I dont know why anyone put up with the nonsense going on in Belisaere, and I am glad she didnt. But it felt like it was incomplete. We didnt actually see Clariel become Chlorr of the Mask. In the end, I still dont understand how she could have made that leap.</span>

<div id="review_1094511720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1094511720" />
    <a title="Wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow"><img alt="Wealhtheow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1094511720?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wealhtheow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wealhtheow" href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=queer-characters">queer-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1094511720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6610040234283411325">Six hundred years before Sabriel was born, the Abhorsen family was large and the Old Kingdom so peaceful that they didn't even bother patrolling it. Clariel is the teenaged daughter of a famed goldsmith and related to both the royal family and the Abhorsen. Her bloodline pulls her into a political battle between the guilds and the king, but her personality draws her toward the solitary peace of the Great Forest. Although she is torn between expectations and her own ambition, Clariel's life narro</span>
  <span id="freeText6610040234283411325" style="display:none">Six hundred years before Sabriel was born, the Abhorsen family was large and the Old Kingdom so peaceful that they didn't even bother patrolling it. Clariel is the teenaged daughter of a famed goldsmith and related to both the royal family and the Abhorsen. Her bloodline pulls her into a political battle between the guilds and the king, but her personality draws her toward the solitary peace of the Great Forest. Although she is torn between expectations and her own ambition, Clariel's life narrows to a single focus when a terrible tragedy strikes her family. Emboldened and enraged, Clariel goes against her family's teachings in her search for vengeance.<br /><br />There are parts of this that I absolutely loved. The action scenes are fantastic and held me riveted. The background characters feel wonderfully unique. Clariel's mother Jaciel turned out to be a particular favorite of mine, an ambitious woman <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who finds calm from her berserker rage in her art <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>--it's a character type I've never seen for a female character before. (Nix's books are always great for inclusion of characters of color and non-standard gender roles. His worlds are proof that it's possible to write fascinating fantasy set in a pre-industrial age and not mirror the same structures of oppression of this one.) Clariel is nearly a great character, but her development near the end is too rushed to truly work for me. I did love that her power comes through her stalwart, obstinate force of will. <br /><br />All in all I enjoyed this, but the final few chapters happened too quickly for my tastes. I wish there'd been more build up of certain things. Afterwards, I realized the legend Clariel left behind and I wished even more that we'd gotten more of her struggle with the Free Magic and less of her lessons in deportment. The chapters in Belisaere felt too detailed and drawn out given how little page time was given to the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[coup and Clariel's ascension to sorcery <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6610040234283411325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jQ6zlQmOrmuZpvtWfGERBQI3zIVZL2kA7TtARcUWJeVfKr1rkUkSLm1vsgKttDHBohmKtVWKYD8oQlmtfn3aGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FoykzGOhx/gBg5n/sIua8ryJ4w07EE/yZQ5cITqnVjzEqKoy+2Z7vfVK0KthXro2HKelPTe1Rs2gd0XJgcypwA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix">About Garth Nix</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207583754p3/8347.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix">Garth Nix
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
11,748
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5688111723595926942">Garth Nix was born in 1963 in Melbourne, Australia, to the sound of the Salvation Army band outside playing 'Hail the Conquering Hero Comes' or possibly 'Roll Out the Barrel'. Garth left Melbourne at an early age for Canberra (the federal capital) and stayed there till he was nineteen, when he left to drive around the UK in a beat-up Austin with a boot full of books and a Silver-Reed typewriter.<br/><br/>De</span>
  <span id="freeText5688111723595926942" style="display:none">Garth Nix was born in 1963 in Melbourne, Australia, to the sound of the Salvation Army band outside playing 'Hail the Conquering Hero Comes' or possibly 'Roll Out the Barrel'. Garth left Melbourne at an early age for Canberra (the federal capital) and stayed there till he was nineteen, when he left to drive around the UK in a beat-up Austin with a boot full of books and a Silver-Reed typewriter.<br /><br />Despite a wheel literally falling off the Austin, Garth survived to return to Australia and study at the University of Canberra. After finishing his degree in 1986 he worked in a bookshop, then as a book publicist, a publisher's sales representative, and editor. Along the way he was also a part-time soldier in the Australian Army Reserve, serving in an Assault Pioneer platoon for four years. Garth left publishing to work as a public relations and marketing consultant from 1994-1997, till he became a full-time writer in 1998. He did that for a year before joining Curtis Brown Australia as a part-time literary agent in 1999. In January 2002 Garth went back to dedicated writer again, despite his belief that full-time writing explains the strange behaviour of many authors.<br /><br />He now lives in Sydney with his wife, two sons and lots of books. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5688111723595926942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

It has been freed from its subterranean prison and now seeks to escape the silver hemispheres, the final barrier to the unleashing of its terrible powers.\n\nOnly Lirael, newly come into her inheritance as the Abhorsen-in-Waiting, has any chance of stopping the Destroyer. She and her companions -- Sam, the Disreputable Dog, and Mogget -- have to take that chance. For the Destroyer is the enemy of all Life, and it must be stopped, though Lirael does not know how.\n\nTo make matters worse, Sam\'s best friend, Nick, is helping the Destroyer, as are the necromancer Hedge and the Greater Dead Chlorr, and there has been no word from the Abhorsen Sabriel or King Touchstone.\n\nEverything depends upon Lirael. A heavy, perhaps even impossible burden for a young woman who just days ago was merely a Second Assistant Librarian. With only a vision from the Clayr to guide her, and the rather mixed help of her companions, Lirael must search in both Life and Death for some means to defeat the Destroyer.\n\nBefore it is too late.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6125574-clariel-the-lost-abhorsen">Quotes from Clariel: The Lost...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I am a great believer that anything not expressly forbidden is explicitly allowed.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1991665-i-am-a-great-believer-that-anything-not-expressly-forbidden">71 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;The most important thing is to be true to yourself, however you feel, and not try to feel or behave differently because you think you should, or someone has told you how you must feel. But do think about it. Unexamined feelings lead to all kinds of trouble.&rdquo;</span>
